<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">The Edge of Glory</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p>"<b>The Edge of Glory</b>" is a song by American singer <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> from her second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">Born This Way</a></i> (2011). The song was released on May 9, 2011 as the album's third single. Initially released as one of two promotional singles for <i>Born This Way</i>, it shortly became a single following its success in digital outlets worldwide. The song was written and produced by Gaga and <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Garibay" title="Fernando Garibay">Fernando Garibay</a>, and is a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> song that speaks of the very last moments of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bmi_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-bmi-1">[1]</a></sup> According to Gaga, lyrical inspiration came from the death of her grandfather, who died in September 2010. Alongside a <a href="/wiki/Saxophone" title="Saxophone">saxophone</a> solo played by the late <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Clemons" title="Clarence Clemons">Clarence Clemons</a>, the melody of the song resembles much of the musical works of <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>, and contains several qualities similar to that of 1980s adult contemporary musical works.</p>
<p>"The Edge of Glory" received critical acclaim, with many reviewers deeming it as an album highlight. Much of the praise went to the song's chorus and the musical production. Reviewers also complimented Gaga's vocals, describing it as "soulful". The song was a commercial success worldwide, charting in the top ten in several major music markets, including Australia, Belgium, Canada, New Zealand, Norway, Spain and the United Kingdom. In the United States, it peaked at number three on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, becoming Gaga's tenth consecutive top-ten single in the United States.</p>
<p>A music video for the song was filmed in late May, co-directed by the singer and her production team, <a href="/wiki/Haus_of_Gaga" title="Haus of Gaga">Haus of Gaga</a>. The video is simple in contrast to much of Gaga's previous work, and portrays her dancing on a fire-escape and walking on a lonely street. Differences include the lack of intricate choreography and back-up dancers, as well as using only one outfit designed by <a href="/wiki/Versace" title="Versace">Versace</a>. Critics lauded the simplicity of the video, while comparing it to the works of <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>. Gaga has performed the song in award shows, music festivals and her concert tours.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_release">Background and release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background and release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG/220px-Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG/330px-Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG/440px-Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clarence_clemons_Olbrich.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Clarence_Clemons" title="Clarence Clemons">Clarence Clemons</a> from <a href="/wiki/E_Street_Band" title="E Street Band">E Street Band</a> played saxophone on "The Edge of Glory".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"The Edge of Glory" was written by Lady Gaga, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Garibay" title="Fernando Garibay">Fernando Garibay</a> and DJ White Shadow, and was produced by Gaga and Garibay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-ET-2">[2]</a></sup> The origins of the song first came about in January 2011, when Gaga released part of the lyrics on her <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-3">[3]</a></sup> White Shadow revealed that before they returned to Europe for the 2010 dates of <a href="/wiki/The_Monster_Ball_Tour" title="The Monster Ball Tour">The Monster Ball Tour</a>, Gaga had taken leave for few days to be with her ailing grandfather. After he died, Gaga told White Shadow that she wrote a song about her grandfather's death and its impact on her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ins_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-ins-4">[4]</a></sup> Gaga spoke to <a href="/wiki/Jon_Pareles" title="Jon Pareles">Jon Pareles</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> about the story behind the song:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"['The Edge of Glory'] was about how when my grandma was standing over my grandfather while he was dying. There was this moment where I felt like he had sort of looked at her and reckoned that he had won in life. Like, 'I'm a champion. We won. Our love made us a winner.' They were married 60 years. I thought about that idea, that the glorious moment of your life is when you decide that it's okay to go, you don’t have any more words to say, more business, more mountains to climb. You're on the cliff, you tip your hat to yourself and you go. That’s what it was for me in that moment when I witnessed it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedom_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>More information in regards to "The Edge of Glory" was revealed by Gaga, in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> where she explained the song as being about one's final moments on earth, before death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-google-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-7">[7]</a></sup> Another inspiration for the song was actor <a href="/wiki/Sylvester_Stallone" title="Sylvester Stallone">Sylvester Stallone</a>'s 1976 film <i><a href="/wiki/Rocky" title="Rocky">Rocky</a></i>, which was Gaga's favorite film. The singer felt that the song was about looking at life directly, with the feeling that he or she is a champion—like the emotion displayed by the character <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Balboa" title="Rocky Balboa">Rocky Balboa</a> in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvuk_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvuk-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 5, 2011, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interscope" title="Interscope">Interscope</a> sent out an e-mail to radio stations across the United States, which stated that "The Edge of Glory" was to be released on Monday, May 9, 2011, as the first of two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Promotional_single" title="Promotional single">promotional single</a> for <i>Born This Way</i>. It was to serve as the first song in the "Countdown to <i>Born This Way</i>" promotion on <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-961kiss_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-961kiss-9">[9]</a></sup> However, after its release to the digital stores, "The Edge of Glory" started selling a considerable amount of digital downloads, prompting Gaga to make it the third single from <i>Born This Way</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbrev_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbrev-11">[11]</a></sup> On her Twitter account Gaga revealed the cover for the single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> It showed Gaga topless with her mouth open, wearing her facial prosthetics from the "<a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(song)" title="Born This Way (song)">Born This Way</a>" cover, and her hair wildly cascading around her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording_and_composition">Recording and composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording and composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_sample.ogg" title="File:Lady Gaga The Edge of Glory sample.ogg">'The Edge of Glory'</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="32.13641723356" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_sample.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">
<source data-bandwidth="58728" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (59 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a8/Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_sample.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'></source></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">A 32-second sample of "The Edge of Glory" featuring the end of the chorus and the beginning of the bridge which contains the saxophone solo. Kevin O'Donnell of <i>Spin</i> compared the composition of the song with <a href="/wiki/Pat_Benatar" title="Pat Benatar">Pat Benatar</a>'s songs, Bonnie Tyler's "<a href="/wiki/Total_Eclipse_of_the_Heart" title="Total Eclipse of the Heart">Total Eclipse of the Heart</a>" (1983) and <a href="/wiki/Laurie_Anderson" title="Laurie Anderson">Laurie Anderson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/O_Superman" title="O Superman">O Superman</a>" (1981).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o.27donnell_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-o.27donnell-14">[14]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>"The Edge of Glory" features synthesizers executed in a style influenced by <a href="/wiki/Smooth_jazz" title="Smooth jazz">smooth jazz</a>, as well as the inclusion of a <a href="/wiki/Saxophone" title="Saxophone">saxophone</a> solo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The song is less electronic and more straightforward pop, and the lyrics deals more of romance than individual inspiration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbrev_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbrev-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvrev_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvrev-16">[16]</a></sup> Garibay revealed that the song was recorded in Gaga's natural vocal tone, and required just one <a href="/wiki/Take#Music" title="Take">take</a>. She requested him to add the sound of <a href="/wiki/Heart_sounds" title="Heart sounds">heartbeat</a> at the start of the track. Garibay said that the decision to add a saxophone solo was a "bold move" for Gaga, since <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_hit_radio" title="Contemporary hit radio">contemporary hit radio</a> did not have any song with a saxophone solo on their song playlists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-record_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-record-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> "The Edge of Glory" opens with Gaga's vocals over a keyboard, singing the line: "There ain't no reason you and me should be alone tonight, yeah baby, tonight, yeah baby."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ins_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-ins-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvrev_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvrev-16">[16]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s Jocelyn Vena, the song's production evokes the late '80s, early '90s adult-contemporary pop, when big <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">choruses</a> were the norm for songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvrev_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtvrev-16">[16]</a></sup> Jason Lipshultz from <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> stated the song "leans upon sunny <a href="/wiki/Electronica" title="Electronica">electronica</a>" that sounds big on the chorus, where Gaga sings "I'm on the edge of glory and I'm hanging on a moment of truth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lipshutzrev_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-lipshutzrev-21">[21]</a></sup> Evan Sawdey of the website <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> found several <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> elements in the composition of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopMatters_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopMatters-22">[22]</a></sup> Vena also felt that what made the song stand out from others on the radio was the saxophone solo by Clemons right in the middle of the track, as Gaga belts out, "I'm on the edge with you."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvrev_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-mtvrev-16">[16]</a></sup> Robert Copsey from <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a> said that the <a href="/wiki/Musical_composition" title="Musical composition">musical composition</a> is a mixture of loud-sounding <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">electric guitars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">club-beat</a> influenced synths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digi_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-digi-23">[23]</a></sup> The song and album ends with a long <a href="/wiki/Coda_(music)" title="Coda (music)">coda</a>, with the sound of the saxophone <a href="/wiki/Fade_(audio_engineering)" title="Fade (audio engineering)">fading out</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedom_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to sheet music published at Musicnotes.com by <a href="/wiki/Sony/ATV_Music_Publishing" title="Sony/ATV Music Publishing">Sony/ATV Music Publishing</a>, "The Edge of Glory" is written in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_time" title="Common time">common time</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> of 128 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beats_per_minute" title="Beats per minute">beats per minute</a>. Set in the <a href="/wiki/Key_(music)" title="Key (music)">key</a> of <a href="/wiki/A_major" title="A major">A major</a>, it follows the basic <a href="/wiki/Chord_progression" title="Chord progression">chord progression</a> of A–E–D for the verse and A–E–F<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;">♯</span>m–D progression for the chorus, while Gaga's voice spans from A<sub>3</sub> to D<sub>5</sub><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheet_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-sheet-24">[24]</a></sup> Gaga's references for the saxophone solo was <a href="/wiki/E_Street_Band" title="E Street Band">E Street Band</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-record_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-record-17">[17]</a></sup> hence she ultimately asked <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Clemons" title="Clarence Clemons">Clarence Clemons</a> from E Street Band to play the instrument. Clemons told <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> that in January 2011, he was contacted by Gaga's management and they wanted him to play on <i>Born This Way</i>. Since the call was on a Friday, Clemons replied that he could record it on the coming Monday or Tuesday, but Gaga was adamant to have him at the New York recording studio on that day itself. Clemons flew from Florida to New York, and reached the recording studio in Manhattan at midnight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exclusive_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-exclusive-25">[25]</a></sup> Gaga wanted him to play saxophone on multiple tracks, one of them being "The Edge of Glory". She simply told Clemons, "We'll put the tape on and you just play". The recording concluded by 3 am in the morning after a few takes. Clemons added that he was surprised to get paid, since he "would have done it for free. I can never believe something that feels so good earns me money."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ins_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-ins-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exclusive_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-exclusive-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"It's the perfect lead-in to closer 'The Edge of Glory,' which sounds exactly like its title, uniting all of Gaga's contradictory impulses in an ecstatic, anthemic, five-minute lunge to the finish line – there's strings and synths, Eurodisco beats and saxophone solos, love and death."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Caryn Ganz of <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> talking about "The Edge of Glory"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpinReview_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-SpinReview-26">[26]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The Edge of Glory was met with general acclaim from critics. While previewing the song Matthew Perpetua from <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> wrote a positive review: "This one sounds crazy in print [...], but somehow it all seems totally natural when you actually hear it." Perpetua added that there is an element of cheesiness in the song, but nevertheless, it is captivating and catchy when one listens to it. He complimented the inclusion of Clemons as an "inspired touch that amplifies the song's Eighties stadium rock vibe," and Clemons' actual performance was described as amazing and among the best of his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-7">[7]</a></sup> In another review, Perpetua noted that "The Edge of Glory" is "an immediate pop anthem".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Fellow <i>Rolling Stone</i> journalist Jody Rosen complimented the hook, the chorus and Clemens' saxophone playing on the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Jocelyn Vena from <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> asserted that the song showed a softer side to Gaga, as opposed to her previous singles from <i>Born This Way</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvrev_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-mtvrev-16">[16]</a></sup> Willa Paskin from <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> was impressed with the track, saying: "If the first two tracks off the forthcoming <i>Born This Way</i> were all jangly dance-rock, this is as smooth as an '80s jam straight off the <a href="/wiki/Flashdance_(soundtrack)" title="Flashdance (soundtrack)"><i>Flashdance</i> soundtrack</a>, and it has the saxophone breakdown to prove it." Paskin also believed that the song had potential to be a summer hit, but could face competition from singer <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>'s single, "<a href="/wiki/Last_Friday_Night_(T.G.I.F.)" title="Last Friday Night (T.G.I.F.)">Last Friday Night (T.G.I.F.)</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga,_Versace.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="509" data-file-width="339" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Lady_Gaga%2C_Versace.jpg/170px-Lady_Gaga%2C_Versace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Lady_Gaga%2C_Versace.jpg/255px-Lady_Gaga%2C_Versace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/Lady_Gaga%2C_Versace.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga,_Versace.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga performing "The Edge of Glory" during <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Ball" title="Born This Way Ball">Born This Way Ball</a> tour in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jason Lipshutz of <i>Billboard</i> wrote that "The Edge of Glory" was "risk-taking, [but] it's focused on romance rather than individual inspiration."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lipshutzrev_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-lipshutzrev-21">[21]</a></sup> Lewis Corner of <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a> awarded the song with five out of five stars and wrote: "Gaga belts over a chorus tastier and more filling than a meatball sub – stuffed with stadium-sized beats and massive techno synths; while the side of sax solo courtesy of the late Clarence Clemons is bound to seduce many a clubber into bringing out their rarely-used-nowadays air sax."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Kevin O'Donnell of <i>Spin</i> noted that in the song, Gaga "goes back to basics". He also called the song a "four-on-the-floor anthem with loads of references to '80s pop music" and concluded "Thankfully, 'Edge of Glory' proves Gaga hasn't let her global celebrity get the best of her art, and she's still capable to cranking out straightforward, dance-ready jams like 'Just Dance' or 'Poker Face'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o.27donnell_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-o.27donnell-14">[14]</a></sup> Both Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> and James Reed of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> praised Clarence Clemons' saxophone solo in "The Edge of Glory".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndependentReview_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-IndependentReview-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nardine Saad from <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> asserted that "The Edge of Glory" was less shock-provoking than her previous releases. Saad also felt that the track was slower and less <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electro</a> in its composition than "<a href="/wiki/Judas_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Judas (Lady Gaga song)">Judas</a>", her then current single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Priya Elan of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> wrote that the song felt like a "pop moment" without Gaga trying too hard to address social issues or religious conflicts; Elan also complimented Clemons' saxophone addition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Similar sentiments were expressed by fellow <i>NME</i> writer Dan Martin, who found the track to be gleaming, calling it the "most ecstatic pop serenade" Gaga has ever come up with.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Robert Copsey from Digital Spy commented that the song is a "straight-up fists-in-the-air feel-good anthem that is less cheesy than 'Born This Way' but equally (if not more) euphoric." However, he found similarity in the <a href="/wiki/Bar_(music)" title="Bar (music)">opening bar</a> of the song with that of <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>'s 2002 single "<a href="/wiki/Song_for_the_Lonely" title="Song for the Lonely">Song for the Lonely</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digi_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-digi-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Megan Gibson from <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> was disappointed with the single, feeling that it was not "particularly good", and called the music as trite, uninspiring and bland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Matthew Cole from <i><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></i> was polarized with the song, stating that while it lowered his expectations for the album, he expressed that the saxophone solo was "admittedly a high point, and one of the more original ideas that Gaga has had of late."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Sal Cinquemani, from the same publication, felt that the song "isn't retro so much as retrograde, starting off with some crafty <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Noise" title="Art of Noise">Art of Noise</a> synth tones before morphing into what sounds like the theme song to an early-'90s sitcom, or an inspirational sports flick, as sung by <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Tyler" title="Bonnie Tyler">Bonnie Tyler</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kot" title="Greg Kot">Greg Kot</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> also gave a mixed review about the song, calling it a "Springsteen-on-steroids bombast" and adding that it features "Clarence Clemons doing almost a parody of a Clarence Clemons sax solo."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChicagoTribuneReview_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChicagoTribuneReview-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"The Edge of Glory" was nominated in the category for Song of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/38th_People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="38th People's Choice Awards">38th People's Choice Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> At the end of 2011, Slant Magazine listed "The Edge of Glory" as the eighth best song of the year, with Ed Gonzalez from the website commenting that the song is "a study in radical contrast that, once you sift aside its deliberately dated effects and the legacy of the late Clarence Clemons, is deep down an incredibly delicate ballad. Yes, everyone expects Gaga to make her confessions on the dance floor, but who knew she could make her shouts whisper?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> It was placed at the same rank by <i>Billboard</i>, and at position seven by <i>Rolling Stone</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In September 2013, the saxophone solo ranked number two on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s list of the 15 Greatest Guest Solos in Rock History.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_performance">Chart performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Chart performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_Europride.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga performing an acoustic version of "The Edge of Glory" on <a href="/wiki/Europride" title="Europride">Europride 2011</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the United States, "The Edge of Glory" debuted at number 31 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40_(Pop_Songs)" title="Mainstream Top 40 (Pop Songs)"><i>Billboard</i> Pop Songs</a> chart, for the issue dated May 28, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popdebut_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-popdebut-45">[45]</a></sup> It also debuted at number two on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Digital_Songs" title="Hot Digital Songs">Hot Digital Songs</a> chart, with sales of 266,000 copies, according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The song entered the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> at number three, and the <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">Radio Songs</a> chart at number 54, with 20 million audience impressions. Gaga became the first artist since <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> to have her first ten singles enter the top ten of the Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hot100debut_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-hot100debut-47">[47]</a></sup> The next week, "The Edge of Glory" moved up to number 18 on Pop Songs, becoming the greatest gainer of the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pop_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-pop-48">[48]</a></sup> However, digital sales dropped by 64% to 98,000 copies, hence the song fell to number 19 on the Hot 100. The song rose to number 37 on the Radio Songs chart, with airplay increasing to 30 million audience impressions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In its third week on the chart, "The Edge of Glory" was again the greatest gaining song on the Pop Songs chart and reached number 14, while debuting at number 33 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adult_Pop_Songs" title="Adult Pop Songs">Adult Pop Songs</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adult_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-adult-50">[50]</a></sup> It was also the greatest gaining digital song, selling 165,000 copies, with overall airplay increasing to 39 million audience impressions, subsequently resulting in the song re-entering the top-ten of the Hot 100 at number eight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In the end, the song reached a peak of number four on Radio Songs, number three on Pop Songs, number one on Hot Dance Club Songs, number seven on Adult Contemporary and number two on Adult Pop Songs. "The Edge of Glory" sold 2.325 million digital copies in 2011 and became the 29th best-selling song of the year in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> As of April 2016, it has sold 3,000,000 digital downloads in the US according to Nielsen SoundScan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ussales_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-ussales-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>"The Edge of Glory" debuted at number three on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a> and entered on the Canadian Hot Digital Songs chart at number two, selling 26,000 digital downloads. It was the top debuting song on the contemporary hit radio chart of Canada, at number 42.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-candebut_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-candebut-54">[54]</a></sup> After four weeks, the song re-entered the top ten of the Canadian Hot 100, and reached the top ten of the Contemporary hit radio chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, "The Edge of Glory" debuted at number six on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uk_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-uk-56">[56]</a></sup> After fluctuating down the charts for few weeks, the song rebounded in the top ten on June 26, 2011. Its digital sales increased by 89.1%, helped by the performance of the song on <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_O%27Grady_Live" title="Paul O'Grady Live">Paul O'Grady Live</a></i>, which was telecast on three occasions, and helped in the radio airplay of the song, where it moved up the chart to reach a peak of eleven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukalbumsales_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukalbumsales-57">[57]</a></sup> As of September 2016, the song has sold 606,000 copies in the UK, and is certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpi_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpi-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uksalesgaga_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-uksalesgaga-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia, it debuted at number 11 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARIA_charts" title="ARIA charts">ARIA Singles Chart</a> and in New Zealand it debuted at number three on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">RIANZ Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aus_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-aus-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nz_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-nz-61">[61]</a></sup> After eleven weeks, the song was certified double platinum and gold by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">Recording Industry Association of New Zealand</a> (RIANZ), for shipment of 140,000 and 7,500 copies of the single, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aria_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-aria-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rianz_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-rianz-63">[63]</a></sup> In Ireland, "The Edge of Glory" debuted at number 10 on the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Singles_Chart" title="Irish Singles Chart">Irish Singles Chart</a>, on May 13, 2011, and reached a peak of four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ire_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-ire-65">[65]</a></sup> In France, the song debuted at number seven on the <a href="/wiki/Syndicat_National_de_l%27%C3%89dition_Phonographique" title="Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique">French Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fra_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-fra-66">[66]</a></sup> In Germany, the song debuted on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_Control_Charts" title="Media Control Charts">Media Control Charts</a> at number 28, and reached a peak of three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ger_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-ger-67">[67]</a></sup> "The Edge of Glory" sold 44,176 digital downloads in South Korea, to debut at number two on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaon_Chart" title="Gaon Chart">Gaon International Online Chart</a> on May 22, 2011, and moved to the top of the chart the next week, with further sales of 48,937 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gaon_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-gaon-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3504" data-file-width="2336" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg/170px-NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg/255px-NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg/340px-NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NYC_-_Buildings_with_fire_exit_ladders_-_0200.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The video featured Gaga dancing outside a <a href="/wiki/Fire_escape" title="Fire escape">fire escape</a> like her early days in New York City</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music_Incorporated" title="Broadcast Music Incorporated">BMI Pop Music Awards</a>, Gaga's choreographer <a href="/wiki/Laurieann_Gibson" title="Laurieann Gibson">Laurieann Gibson</a> said that they would be filming the <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for "The Edge of Glory" soon. While she did not reveal much about the music video concept, she added: "I just know that we'll be feeling very fishy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Gaga told <a href="/wiki/MTV_(UK_and_Ireland)" title="MTV (UK and Ireland)">MTV UK</a> that she had already written the treatment for the video, adding that it's her favorite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvuk_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvuk-8">[8]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E!_Online" title="E! Online">E! Online</a> reported that a casting call for the video was made, where the agents looked for a Puerto Rican or Dominican origin male. Other roles included a male or female on-air reporter, a doctor role reminiscent to the one in the American show <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._90210" title="Dr. 90210">Dr. 90210</a></i>, and a group of military men for scenes involving rifles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The music video director was confirmed as <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kahn" title="Joseph Kahn">Joseph Kahn</a>, but Interscope Records later confirmed that Kahn and Gaga parted ways due to collaborative misunderstandings. Gibson confirmed that there was "some issues on the set", which resulted in Kahn being replaced as the director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga's creative team <a href="/wiki/Haus_of_Gaga" title="Haus of Gaga">Haus of Gaga</a> were later chosen to direct the video instead. Chancler Haynes, Kahn's on-set editor revealed that the mermaid-themed performance of the song, on <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Grand_Journal_(Canal%2B)" title="Le Grand Journal (Canal+)">Le Grand Journal</a></i> was the actual theme of the video, and included sets built for a hospital scene, Brooklyn Bridge, and a big underwater mermaid scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypostvideo_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-nypostvideo-72">[72]</a></sup> However, at the last minute before shooting, Gaga changed her mind regarding the whole concept, leading to a disagreement with Kahn, and hence it was cancelled. She then shot the scenes with <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Clemons" title="Clarence Clemons">Clarence Clemons</a> in a New York City set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypostvideo_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-nypostvideo-72">[72]</a></sup> She later explained that her idea was to create a "sweater set of a video". She wanted to acknowledge herself and the success she had experienced in her music career, with a simplified video showing her dancing outside her New York apartment from her early days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The music video premiered on June 16, 2011, on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/So_You_Think_You_Can_Dance_(season_8)" title="So You Think You Can Dance (season 8)">eighth season</a> of US reality television show, <i><a href="/wiki/So_You_Think_You_Can_Dance_(U.S._TV_series)" title="So You Think You Can Dance (U.S. TV series)">So You Think You Can Dance</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gaga's wardrobe throughout the entire video primarily consists of only one outfit which was designed by <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Versace" title="Gianni Versace">Gianni Versace</a>. The dress consists of a <a href="/wiki/Sadomasochism" title="Sadomasochism">S&amp;M</a> inspired outfit, with heavy gold jewelry, studs on the leather, and vibrant nail polish and lipstick. Notable in the video is the absence of back-up dancers, elaborate choreography, or a symbolic plot: components that have all been predominant in Gaga's other music videos. Aside from Gaga herself, Clemons is the only other person to appear in the video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slant_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-slant-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The video begins with Gaga slowly appearing from behind a building on a deserted street corner. The whole scenario is bathed in red and violet lights, coming from the windows of the buildings and alleyways as steam billows out from the drains. When the first verse of the song begins, Gaga emerges from the window of an apartment onto the fire escape. A long take follows, of Gaga strutting through the red-lit district singing the line "I got a reason that you should take me home tonight", and a shock of black hair falls in her eyes. Gaga does not remove it and the shot spans to her walking backside, gesturing the viewer to follow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slant_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-slant-75">[75]</a></sup> The video consists mostly of interchanging shots of Gaga dancing and singing on the street, on the fire escape, and on the steps in front of the apartment building with Clemons. Near the end of the video, after Clemons' saxophone solo, Gaga crouches in front of the building's steps and kisses the sidewalk. The video concludes with a close-up of Gaga's face, before she re-enters through the window into her smokey apartment.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:288px;max-width:288px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1710" data-file-width="1122" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/130px-Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/195px-Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/260px-Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michaeljackson_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="490" data-file-width="379" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Michaeljackson_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Michaeljackson_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Michaeljackson_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Michaeljackson_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Michaeljackson_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Michaeljackson_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Several critics opined that some scenes in the music video were reminiscent to <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s music video for "<a href="/wiki/Papa_Don%27t_Preach" title="Papa Don't Preach">Papa Don't Preach</a>", and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s music video for "<a href="/wiki/Billie_Jean" title="Billie Jean">Billie Jean</a>".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Both Jocelyn Vena from MTV and Christian Blauvelt from <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> commented on the similarity of the music video with the Broadway musical, <i><a href="/wiki/Rent_(musical)" title="Rent (musical)">Rent</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvvideo_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvvideo-76">[76]</a></sup> Vena also compared the visuals with those for <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s 1986 single "<a href="/wiki/Papa_Don%27t_Preach" title="Papa Don't Preach">Papa Don't Preach</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s 1984 single, "<a href="/wiki/Billie_Jean" title="Billie Jean">Billie Jean</a>". She concluded by saying that the music video "still manages to shine, mostly because of its simplicity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvvideo_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvvideo-76">[76]</a></sup> In another review, James Montgomery from MTV, also found similarities between the video and the musicals <i>Rent</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/West_Side_Story" title="West Side Story">West Side Story</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Blauvelt was initially surprised to see the simplistic approach of the video, since her previous releases had provocative visuals. He added that the video seemed a "clear homage" to Gaga's inspirations like Madonna, concluding that "all the references in 'The Edge of Glory' are so overt, there's no way it could be shameless cribbing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sal Cinquemani of <i>Slant Magazine</i> gave the video a positive review, calling it a "visual triumph", with "breathtaking" art direction, and a "gray-blue-black color palette carefully calibrated by Gaga's vibrant lipstick and nail polish, a red painted stripe on the curb, and the gold of her jewelry and the studs on her leather, not to mention Clarence Clemons's brass." The video was compared to Michael Jackson's "<a href="/wiki/The_Way_You_Make_Me_Feel" title="The Way You Make Me Feel">The Way You Make Me Feel</a>," <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/When_I_Think_of_You" title="When I Think of You">When I Think of You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Pleasure_Principle_(song)" title="The Pleasure Principle (song)">The Pleasure Principle</a>", and the film, <i><a href="/wiki/Crimes_of_Passion_(1984_film)" title="Crimes of Passion (1984 film)">Crimes of Passion</a></i>, all of them being 1980s videos and films. He did, however, criticize Gaga's "half-convincing" lip-synching.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slant_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-slant-75">[75]</a></sup> Writing for <i>The Washington Post</i>, Sarah Anne Hughes called the video "shockingly simple".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washpost_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-washpost-79">[79]</a></sup> Amos Barshad from <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> liked the straight approach Gaga took with the video, and although he called it boring compared to Gaga's previous efforts, he felt the video worked well because of the simplicity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jarett Wieselman from <i>New York Post</i> tried to understand what actually went wrong with the production, and came to the conclusion that the mutual disagreements between Gaga and Kahn led to the video being a "piece of rubbish". He deemed the whole issue surrounding the production as "foolish", in the end agreeing that "it was foolish of us to expect that GaGa would never stumble because, despite the preternatural image constantly presented, she is only human after all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypostvideo_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-nypostvideo-72">[72]</a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Daniel Kreps gave a mixed review of the video, calling the song "over-the-top" with a "lackluster" and "understated" video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Dose_(magazine)" title="Dose (magazine)">Dose</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Leah Collins was more neutral in her review, questioning if Gaga was simply "swooning with nostalgia for other pop culture nuggets that have featured the same NYC backdrop of fire escapes and brown-stone steps" or just attempting to "be saving a metric buttload on the budget".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dose_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dose-82">[82]</a></sup> While reviewing the video for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Vancouver_Sun" title="The Vancouver Sun">The Vancouver Sun</a></i>, Collins compared Gaga's look in the video to a "hooker" from the 1982 American <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> film, <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="903" data-file-width="933" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_The_Edge_of_Glory_GMA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga performing "The Edge of Glory" on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> as a part of their "Summer Concert Series"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gaga first performed an acoustic-jazz version of the song at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_1%27s_Big_Weekend" title="Radio 1's Big Weekend">Radio 1's Big Weekend</a> in <a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle, Cumbria</a> on May 15, 2011. During the song, she revealed that her record company had told her to keep new material to a minimum, but she said she wanted to air the track in full.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Another piano version of the song was performed on May 21, 2011, on the <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live_(season_36)" title="Saturday Night Live (season 36)">season finale</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, where Gaga wore a metallic black dress, knee-high boots and a semi-circular metallic headdress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The full version was first performed at the final show of <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_10)" title="American Idol (season 10)"><i>American Idol</i> season 10</a> on May 25, 2011, where she was joined by Clemons in person. Gaga appeared perched atop a mountain top on the "Idol" stage, dressed in a long cape and a bedazzled headpiece. A trio of dancers were at the base of the set performing choreographed dance steps while Gaga sang from the top. At the end of the performance, Gaga and a dancer embraced each other, took a breath and then jumped off the edge of the stage, landing out of sight on a bed of fake rocks, as steam shot up high in the air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvai_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvai-86">[86]</a></sup> Len Melisurgo from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Star-Ledger" title="The Star-Ledger">The Star-Ledger</a></i> felt that the performance was too "sexually suggestive" for the audience of <i>American Idol</i> and wondered whether Gaga "went just a little too far for a family-oriented show that's geared toward a younger audience?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Conversely, Adam Graham from MTV News listed it as one of Gaga's most memorable television performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvai_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvai-86">[86]</a></sup> Monica Herrera from <i>Billboard</i> listed it as the fourth best performance of the night, and felt that Gaga "channeled <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>" in her personality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 27, 2011, Gaga performed "The Edge of Glory" on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> as a part of their "Summer Concert Series", wearing a full black dress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germany%27s_Next_Topmodel,_Cycle_6" title="Germany's Next Topmodel, Cycle 6">sixth cycle</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Germany%27s_Next_Topmodel" title="Germany's Next Topmodel">Germany's Next Topmodel</a></i>, Gaga performed the song on the final show. The performance included a segment where Gaga was portrayed as getting beheaded in a <a href="/wiki/Guillotine" title="Guillotine">guillotine</a>. Gaga then jumped up with a prosthetic head held aloft, before snarling towards the judges "I would kill for fashion". The whole show was broadcast worldwide on the internet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> An acoustic version was later performed at the <a href="/wiki/Europride" title="Europride">Europride 2011</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, along with "Born This Way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> At the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X_Factor_(France)" title="X Factor (France)">X Factor</a></i> show in Paris, Gaga performed it along with "<a href="/wiki/Judas_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Judas (Lady Gaga song)">Judas</a>". She wore a fringed dress with long hair extensions and a long blue wig, while playing a <a href="/wiki/Keytar" title="Keytar">keytar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> At the French television show, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Grand_Journal_(Canal%2B)" title="Le Grand Journal (Canal+)">Le Grand Journal</a></i>, a mermaid themed performance of "The Edge of Glory" was televised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypostvideo_72-3"><a href="#cite_note-nypostvideo-72">[72]</a></sup> Gaga re-created the New York City fire escape sets for the performance of the song on the <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_O%27Grady_Live" title="Paul O'Grady Live">Paul O'Grady Live</a></i> show. Ryan Love of Digital Spy had an advance preview of the recording of the show, and complimented the choreography by Gaga and her dancer, during the saxophone interlude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paul_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-paul-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga opened the <a href="/wiki/2011_MuchMusic_Video_Awards" title="2011 MuchMusic Video Awards">2011 MuchMusic Video Awards</a> with a performance of the song, sporting a bejeweled catsuit and a bob teal colored wig.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> While on tour in Japan, Gaga performed "The Edge of Glory" and "Born This Way" at the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Aid_Japan" title="2011 MTV Video Music Aid Japan">2011 MTV Video Music Aid Japan</a>. She started the performance while hanging from a giant <a href="/wiki/Spider_web" title="Spider web">spider web</a>, with her aquamarine hair extensions stuck in it. Beginning to sing, Gaga pulled and tugged at the web, and ultimately broke free to join her dancers as she finished the performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> On October 16, 2011 she performed the song during a concert at the Hollywood Bowl in Los Angeles for the <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Foundation" title="Clinton Foundation">Clinton Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> She performed the song as the encore to her 2012 <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Ball" title="Born This Way Ball">Born This Way Ball</a> tour in which she plays the beginning of the song on piano atop a watch tower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_versions">Cover versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Edge_of_Glory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cover versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>American pop singer <a href="/wiki/Nick_Jonas" title="Nick Jonas">Nick Jonas</a> sang an acoustic version of the song in July during his concert at the <a href="/wiki/Westfield_Century_City" title="Westfield Century City">Westfield Century City</a> in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonascover_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-jonascover-98">[98]</a></sup> Before the performance Jonas announced: "Do you guys mind if I play a couple of songs I like from pop radio right now? Would that be OK? The only problem is, I don't know all the words. So if you know them, sing along."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonascover_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-jonascover-98">[98]</a></sup> After watching the performance online, Gaga posted his cover on her Twitter account along with the words "Swoon! Nick Jonas singing The Edge of Glory. On my way to press conference in Taichung, listening to it. So dreamy! X."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonascover_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-jonascover-98">[98]</a></sup> British band <a href="/wiki/Friendly_Fires" title="Friendly Fires">Friendly Fires</a> covered the song during <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Live_Lounge" title="Live Lounge">Live Lounge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Kevin O'Donnell of <i>Spin</i> praised their cover writing: "Gaga's original showcases the pop star's gale force pipes, and Friendly Fires frontman Ed Macfarlane doesn't try to match that energy. Instead, they offer a lovely, cinematic take on the song: Macfarlane croons with the heart-on-sleeve sensitivity of an <a href="/wiki/Emo" title="Emo">emo</a>-boy over cascading synth melodies and a breezy funk pulse. Nice!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
